## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science & solid mechanics (constitutive stress–strain–temperature modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables map directly to constitutive behavior of solids: stress (sigma) as a function of strain (epsilon) with temperature (T) dependence through elastic modulus, yield/flow stress, and thermal softening. Common models combine linear/nonlinear elasticity with temperature-dependent parameters and sometimes smooth yield-like transitions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (1D linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear thermoelastic stiffness): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (E varies approximately linearly with T over a range)
- Exponential modulus softening: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (strong temperature sensitivity of stiffness)
- Polynomial nonlinearity (hyperelastic-like expansion): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elasticity at moderate strain)
- Temperature-scaled nonlinear elasticity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (nonlinear elastic response with T-dependent coefficients)
- Power-law hardening (Hollomon-type in plastic region): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (work hardening when strain is the main driver)
- Temperature-dependent strength coefficient (thermal softening of hardening law): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (strength drops/increases with T while hardening persists)
- Ramberg–Osgood inversion-like stress form (smooth elastic–plastic transition): sigma = c0 * epsilon / (c1 + epsilon**c2) (captures initial linearity and later deviation without a sharp yield point)
- Smooth yield transition (tanh-based): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * tanh(c3 * epsilon) (elastic + saturating plastic contribution; smooth yielding)
- Thermal-softening multiplier on a base curve: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2) * (c3 + c4 * exp(c5 * T)) (separable strain-shape times temperature factor)
- Coupled rational thermo-mechanical form: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2) / (c3 + c4 * T) (effective softening with increasing T; convenient empirical fit)
- Johnson–Cook-like structure (strain hardening × thermal softening, simplified without strain-rate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T + c5 * T**2) (engineering plasticity with explicit thermal softening polynomial)
- Viscoplastic/creep-inspired exponential-in-stress inversion surrogate (empirical stress surface): sigma = c0 + c1 * log(c2 + epsilon) + c3 * T (often used as a regression-friendly surrogate for creep/flow surfaces)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain elasticity → sigma proportional to epsilon; temperature enters by making the proportionality (modulus) a function of T.
- Thermal softening of stiffness/strength → multiplicative factors that decrease with T (often linear or exponential in T) applied to an epsilon-dependent base curve.
- Work hardening in plasticity → power laws in epsilon (epsilon**c) or added polynomial terms in epsilon; typically monotone increasing in epsilon.
- Smooth elastic–plastic transition (no sharp yield in data) → tanh(c*epsilon), log(c+epsilon), or rational forms that are linear near epsilon≈0 and deviate gradually.
- Separable effects (common engineering approximation) → sigma ≈ f(epsilon) * g(T), capturing that temperature scales the whole stress–strain curve.
- Curvature changes with temperature → allow T-dependent coefficients on epsilon, epsilon**2, etc., rather than only a global multiplier.
- Avoiding nonphysical negative stresses at small strain → use forms that ensure sigma→0 as epsilon→0 (e.g., sigma proportional to epsilon times a bounded modifier).
- High-temperature regime dominance → include higher-order T terms (T**2, T**3) when softening accelerates with temperature.
- Empirical constitutive surfaces → rational functions in T (e.g., divide by (c+T)) to represent diminishing stress capacity as temperature rises without requiring an explicit melt temperature.

GT Equivalence Verification (MatSci23)

GT: c0*epsilon**c1*exp(-c2/(c3*T)) - c4*(T - c5) + c6*(T - c7)*log(epsilon + c8)
Candidate formulas: 50

Let  
\[
\text{GT}(\epsilon,T)=A\,\epsilon^{p}\exp(-B/T)\;-\;D\,(T-T_0)\;+\;E\,(T-T_0)\log(\epsilon+1)
\]
with fixed values \(A=64.9458\), \(p=0.6137\), \(B=36.9451/8.314\), \(D=0.214822\), \(E=3.55398\), \(T_0=331.6841\).  
Key structural facts:

- GT has an **Arrhenius-in-1/T** term: \(\epsilon^{p}\exp(-B/T)\) (not \(\exp(kT)\)).
- GT has a **linear-in-\(T\)** part with an \(\epsilon\)-dependent slope: \((T-T_0)\big(-D+E\log(\epsilon+1)\big)\).
- Expanding the last two terms: \(-D T + D T_0 + E T\log(\epsilon+1) - E T_0\log(\epsilon+1)\). So GT contains **both** \(T\log(\epsilon+1)\) and \(\log(\epsilon+1)\) (with fixed coupling via the same \(T_0\)).

A candidate can match if it can produce exactly these dependencies (possibly after setting some coefficients to 0), at least on a plausible domain (e.g., \(\epsilon\ge 0\) to handle Abs/Max).

### 1
Has \(\epsilon^{c3}\exp(Tc4)\) and \(\exp(Tc8)\log(\cdot)\): exponentials in \(T\), not \(\exp(\text{const}/T)\). Also lacks a \((T-T_0)\) factor structure. **No.**

I need to analyze each candidate to determine if it can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `64.95*epsilon^0.614*exp(-36.95/(8.314*T)) - 0.2148*(T - 331.68) + 3.554*(T - 331.68)*log(epsilon + 1)`

Let me expand the GT:
- `64.95*epsilon^0.614*exp(-4.443/T)` [since 36.95/8.314 ≈ 4.443]
- `- 0.2148*T + 0.2148*331.68`
- `+ 3.554*T*log(epsilon+1) - 3.554*331.68*log(epsilon+1)`

So GT = `64.95*epsilon^0.614*exp(-4.443/T) - 0.2148*T + 71.25 + 3.554*T*log(epsilon+1) - 1178.8*log(epsilon+1)`

The key structural components are:
1. `epsilon^c * exp(c/T)` — Arrhenius-like term
2. `T` — linear in T
3. Constant term
4. `T*log(epsilon+1)` — T times log term
5. `log(epsilon+1)` — standalone log term

Let me check each candidate for these basis functions:

**Candidate 1:** `T*c0 + c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon^c3*exp(T*c4) + c5*log(c6*epsilon+1) + c7*exp(T*c8)*log(c9*epsilon+1)`

Has `exp(T*c4)` not `exp(c/T)`. These are fundamentally different functions. The GT needs `exp(c/T)` which cannot be matched by `exp(c*T)`.
Also needs `T*log(epsilon+1)` — has `exp(T*c8)*log(...)` which is not `T*log(...)`.
